<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M1](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m001.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Crab Nebula, Taurus A</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">P Neb</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Tau</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">8.4</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> ~8/07</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

 Very, very, very, very dim in 6" at RPI.  Remnant of supernova of 1054\. This is a somewhat difficult object at RPI, due to being large and diffuse. It is best viewed in the 16", when high in the sky and  fills up a good portion of the 50mm. Rocking the telescope helps.

</td>

</tr>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Satellite Of Andromeda Galaxy</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Galaxy</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">And</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">9.1</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> 7/07</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

Appears as star w/ slight nebulosity in 6". Easily discernable in 16" Cas 

</td>

</tr>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 37; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 37; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 8.0pt;">Triangulum Galaxy, Pinwheel Galaxy</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 37; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Galaxy</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 37; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 37; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">6.2</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 37; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Spiral Cluster</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

</td>

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">6</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> </span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom"></td>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M35](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m035.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">M35,NGC2168</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Gem</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">5.5</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> 3/22/09</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

Another excellent open cluster. Starfield fills the entire FOV of the 50mm in the 16". It is nice to compare M35-M38 because they are quite close to each other in the sky. It has over 120 stars brighter than mag 13 and around 500 total, spread over an area the size of the full moon.

</td>

</tr>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M36](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m036.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Pinwheel Cluster</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Aur</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">6.5</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">  2/13/09</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

There are 3 clusters lying fairly close together in Auiga, M36, 37 and 38\. This one is the most sparse. It is primarily a few dozen bright stars, perhaps of slightly different hues (yellow-orange). Otherwise, not terribly interesting, and I don't see why its called the pinwheel..

</td>

</tr>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 43; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M37](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m037.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Aur</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">6</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">  2/13/09</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 43; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

Very nice open cluster. A rich field of dim stars sprinkled like salt (and pepper?). Fairly large cluster (easily fills 50mm in 16"). Worth seeing in finder scope as well.

</td>

</tr>

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M38](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m038.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Starfish Cluster</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Aur</span></span>

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">7</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 28; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 28; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Cyg</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 28; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">5.5</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 28; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> </span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 28; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom"></td>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M40](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m040.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Winnecke 4</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Dbl+Asterism</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Uma</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">8.7</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">2/14/09 </span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

This object is a rather uninteresting double star as the separation is not very close. It is believed to in fact be an optical double. Measurements show the stars are moving apart, and have moved significantly in the last century. In all likelihood, this was a mistake in Messer's list, he was trying to find a non-existent nebula reported to be near this double. (see link for more info).

</td>

</tr>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M41](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m041.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Little Beehive</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Cma</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">5</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> </span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

Basically a smaller Beehive. As the Beehive is a massive cluster, this object is still pretty big, and best viewed through finder scope to get the proper view.  May have been recorded by Aristotle in 325 B.C

</td>

</tr>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M42](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m042.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Great Orion Nebula, Orion A</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Open+D Neb</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Ori</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">4</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> 2006?</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

(first viewed w/ naked eye, unknown time)

 Best nebula in N. Hemisphere. !!! Trapezium easily seen in 6" and 16" Cas. Texturing and outer diffuse glow visible in 16"

</td>

</tr>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M43](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m043.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">De Mairan's Nebula</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">D Neb</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Ori</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">9</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> 11/21</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

This is basically an extension of the Orion Nebula. There is a bright star adjacent to M42 with faint nebulosity around it. Both this and the center of the Orion Nebula can fit in the same FOV in the 16".

</td>

</tr>

<tr style="height: 14.05pt;">

<td style="width: 48; height: 27; border-left: 1.0pt solid black; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M44](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m044.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">4</span></span>

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">4/29/08</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

Relatively faint galaxy, but able to spot with 50mm in 16".  Imaged.  Saw again on a dark night 2/14/09, and noted that this is a fairly large galaxy, just as big as M80 or M81.

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> 2/21/09</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

Pretty big cluster, fills 50mm. Has about 10 bright stars, and many dim ones. (Actual count is around 500 stars).  It is about the age of our solar system, which is old for an open cluster, and therefore contains a fair number of red giants.

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> 2008</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

Excellent Galaxy for 16". This is a relatively low integrated magnitude, but it is a quite small, compact object, so it is easily seen.

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M78](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m078.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">M78,NGC2068</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 99; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">D Neb</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 40; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Ori</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">8</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> </span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

This object is sort of a mystery to me... it is apparently part of an array of reflection nebula in the Orion complex, and the brightest reflection nebula in the N. Hemisphere. It lies above the leftmost star in Orion's belt. It should be very easy to spot under dark skies, but I'm not really sure of the scale of the thing. Starry night shows it being as very small, but it is listed as 8x6 arc mins and looks pretty big.

</td>

</tr>

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">Leo</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 33; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt;">10.6</span></span>

</td>

<td style="width: 65; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

<span style="font-family: Verdana;"> 2/14/09</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 240; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" align="left" valign="bottom">

M95 and M96 are both excellent galaxies. Despite a low integrated magnitude, these objects where relatively easy to spot, given a clear, dark night. This is probably because they are relatively small.  Both can be seen in the 50mm eyepiece at the same time, and its quite a sight to see.

</td>

</tr>

<span style="font-family: Verdana;">[M96](http://www.maa.clell.de/Messier/E/m096.html)</span>

</td>

<td style="width: 173; height: 27; border-left: medium none; border-right: 1.0pt solid black; border-top: medium none; border-bottom: 1.0pt solid black; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top">

**<span style="font-size: large;">Planets & Moons</span>**

<div align="center">

<center>

<table style="border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" width="61%" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0">

<tbody>

<tr>

<td width="7%" height="18">**Planet**</td>

<td width="9%" height="18">**Mag**</td>

<td width="8%" height="18">**Date**</td>

<tr>

<td width="7%" height="25">Mercury</td>

<td width="9%" height="25">-1.9</td>

<td width="8%" height="25">11/08</td>

<td width="28%" height="25"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Was walking back to car at Highland Meadows when I happened to see Mercury by chance during a conjunction with Jupiter at sunset. (A very striking combination.. which I verified afterwards with Starry Night). This is a rather tricky object to view.. you have to be somewhere with an open western horizon at just the right time after sunset... or get up really early in the morning and have a clear eastern horizon. I hope to observe again through telescope during maximum elongation.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="7%" height="18">Venus</td>

<td width="9%" height="18">-3.7 - -4.7</td>

<td width="8%" height="18">?</td>

<td width="28%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Varies in size and brightness. Not much to see other than phases. Have not yet seen the "Ashen glow" phenomena. I have not been able to see it with the naked eye during the day, but others have. This is a good object to view with the 16" during Solar Observing, if there are large crowds. During March 2009, we were able to discern the crescent shape with the naked eye.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="7%" height="18">Earth</td>

<td width="9%" height="18">7 - -26.73</td>

<td width="8%" height="18">3/6/88</td>

<td width="28%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Don't forget Earth!</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="7%" height="18">Mars</td>

<td width="9%" height="18">1.8 - -2.91</td>

<td width="8%" height="18">?</td>

<td width="28%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">I haven't had much success with Mars... it looks nice and red.. but otherwise quite disappointing. Its a shame, because its my favorite planet (after Earth of course).</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="7%" height="18">Jupiter</td>

<td width="9%" height="18">-1.6 - -2.94</td>

<td width="8%" height="18">?</td>

<td width="28%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Cloud bands and great red spot visible in 6" along with 4 Galilean moons. Shadow of Io was visible in 6" at ADK star party. Shadow has also been observed in 16". Very good object for 16" once it gets high in the sky. </span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="7%" height="18">Saturn</td>

<td width="9%" height="18">+1.2 - -0.24</td>

<td width="8%" height="18">?</td>

<td width="28%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Most viewed planet. Great object in 16". Have seen Cassini division several times under good conditions as well as 5 brightest moons, Titan, Tethys, Dione, Rhea and Iapetus.</span></td>

</tr>

**<span style="font-size: large;">Comets</span>**

<div align="center">

<center>

<table style="border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" width="60%" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0">

<tbody>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="1">**Name**</td>

<td width="4%" height="1">**Mag**</td>

<td width="1%" height="1">**Date**</td>

<td width="43%" height="1">**Notes**</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="1">[17P/Holmes](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet_Holmes)</td>

<td width="4%" height="1">2.8-3</td>

<td width="1%" height="1">10/11/08</td>

<td width="43%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Normally dim comet which had spectacular outburst. Visible with naked eye for several weeks. It appeared as a star with nebulosity at first, but eventually expanded and lost brightness, eventually it was half the size of moon. The bright core was easily visible in 16" a few days after the outburst. Slight fragmentation may have been observed around the nucleus, although this was never confirmed. (Technically, the nucleolus is too small to be visible, what one sees is an bright inner coma). The overall halo structure was easily seen in binoculars and very impressive in the 3" finder.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="23">

# <span style="font-weight: 400;"><span style="font-size: medium;">[C/2007 N3 Lulin](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C/2007_N3)</span></span>

 </td>

<td width="4%" height="23">~7-8</td>

<td width="1%" height="23">2/24/09</td>

<td width="43%" height="23"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Many hoped that Comet Lulin would reach naked eye visibility. In the end it was not quite bright enough, except under perfectly dark skies. At RPI  there was no chance of visual observation but it could be seen fairly easily with binoculars. I first spotted it with Dave's 10" lying just above Saturn. As the night progressed it moved quite noticeably on a path from Saturn towards Regulus. It was quite bright in the 16", but it did not have very much of a comet-like appearance; appearing as a bright cloud with a semi-circular coma. After careful inspection, it was clear that coma was in fact elliptical and extending off both sides.  This overall indistinctness of the tail was due to the fact that the comet was moving towards us in the plane of the earth's orbit, and the tail was fanning out behind it. A subsequent observation was made that Saturday, 3/1/09 and it had dimmed quite noticeably in the 16". By that time it had already passed Regulus and was headed through Cancer towards Gemini. I observed it again on 3/20/09 while it was in Gemini , and it had dimmed down to magnitude 8.6 but was still fairly easy to spot in the 16". It had shrunk to at most half, maybe a quarter of its original size, and appeared a little bit more elongated. Still, it was very dim and fuzzy, and there was nothing about it by which was distinctly cometary in nature.  We had to check to make sure we were not actually looking at a globular cluster or galaxy that happened to be nearby.</span></td>

</tr>

</tbody>

</table>

</center>

</div>

<span style="font-size: large;">**Spacecraft**</span>

<div align="center">

<center>

<table style="border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" width="60%" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0">

<tbody>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="1">**Name**</td>

<td width="5%" height="1">**Mag**</td>

<td width="5%" height="1">**Date**</td>

<td width="39%" height="1">**Notes**</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="1">[Iridium Flares](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iridium_flare)</td>

<td width="5%" height="1">-1to -8</td>

<td width="5%" height="1">various</td>

<td width="39%" height="1"> 

Iridium Flares are really cool! On at least one occasion I saw one reach magnitude -8, which is about as bright as they get.

</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="23">

#   
<span style="font-size: medium;"><span style="font-weight: 400;">[International Space Station](http://heavens-above.com)</span></span>

</td>

<td width="5%" height="23">-1 to -2 in 2007

-2 to -3 in 2009

</td>

<td width="5%" height="23">Various</td>

<td width="39%" height="23">The ISS is very easy to see, and always a crowd pleaser.</td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="23">

#   
<span style="font-size: medium;"><span style="font-weight: 400;">[Space Shuttle Discovery](http://www.space.com/spacewatch/090310-space-shuttle-launch-spotting.html) (during launch)</span></span>

</td>

<td width="5%" height="23">around 0 to -1</td>

<td width="5%" height="23">3-15-09</td>

<td width="39%" height="23">  
We had a special opportunity to view the Shuttle Launch, because it was an evening launch with clear skies. I was skeptical about whether we would see it from the Hirsch Observatory, and quite amazed when we did. The shuttle launched right on time at 7:43, which we watched indoors on NASA TV. Then we went out onto the roof and stood scanning the southern horizon with no avail. We had just about given up when a bright red glow object appeared moving very fast starting in the southeast. It flickered on and off several times. We later determined this must have been due to a large complex of clouds just south of Long Island. We tracked the shuttle for about 30 seconds before main-engine cut off.  
 </td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="4%" height="23">

#   
<span style="font-size: medium;"><span style="font-weight: 400;">[Space Shuttle Discovery](http://www.space.com/spacewatch/090310-space-shuttle-launch-spotting.html) (In orbit)</span></span>

</td>

<td width="5%" height="23">around 2.5-3</td>

<td width="5%" height="23">3-28-09</td>

<td width="39%" height="23">  
I was standing out on the roof when I noticed 2 objects moving along the same arc in the North. The first was quite bright, and due to the gentle curve of the arc, I immediately suspected it was the ISS, rather than a plane. The other object was about 1-1.5 degrees away, leading the ISS. I was very sure that was the shuttle, but others were skeptical. A quick check online showed that the shuttle had undocked from the ISS about 6 hours ago.   
 </td>

</tr>

</tbody>

</table>

</center>

</div>

information I know of is not Wikipedia, it is the [NGC/IC Project](http://www.ngcic.org/pubdb.htm).  
However, due to the site design, I was not able to link directly to pages there.

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="20">[Albireo](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albireo)</td>

<td width="9%" height="20"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Beta Cygni</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="20"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Double Star</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="20"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">3&5</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="20"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2007</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="20"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Part of Cygnus, a bright double star with red and blue components. Imaged.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="18">[Coathanger Cluster](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coathanger_cluster)</td>

<td width="9%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Collinder 399</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Asterism</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">3.6</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2008</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Also known as Brocchi's Cluster, it is an asterism (chance alignment), not a star cluster. It consists of 6 stars in a straight line, and a few other stars composing the hook of the "coathanger".</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="1">[Double Double](Epsilon%20Lyre) </td>

<td width="9%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Epsilon Lyrae</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Multiple Star</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">1.1</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2007</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Cool double double star. The first split can be seen with binoculars. The second split can be resolved in the 11" and the 16".</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="1">[Gamma Andromeda](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamma_Andromedae)</td>

<td width="9%" height="1"> </td>

<td width="9%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Double Star</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="1"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-2.9</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="1"> </td>

<td width="119%" height="1"> </td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="18">[Kite Cluster](http://www.skyhound.com/sh/archive/dec/NGC_1664.html)</td>

<td width="9%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">NGC 1664</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Open Cluster</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">7.2</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">8/22/08</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="18"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This is a small open cluster. The brightest stars resembled a diamond or "kite". The density of surrounding stars did not seem above normal, so it seemed like more like an asterism to me. Observed at ADK star party.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[The Mexican Jumping Star](http://www.seds.org/messier/xtra/ngc/n2362.html)</td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">NGC 2362 Tau Canis Majoris Cluster</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Open cluster + visual double</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">4.1</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2/14/09</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This one certainly has an interesting name. It is a typical open cluster.. has around 60 stars and a very faint nebula surrounding it which we could not see.  The brightest star, Tau Canis Majoris, is right in the center and shines in bright blue at magnitude 4.39\. It is the brighter component of a spectroscopic binary. But, more interestingly, it is also part of a visual binary with a nearby star. We were not able to split this visual binary, so when looking at it, there definitely did seem to be something peculiar about it.. at times it appears to have an oblong shape.. due to the second star right nearby. This is probably why its called the "Mexican Jumping Star".</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[Mizor and Alcor](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mizar_(star))</td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">"The Horse and Rider"</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Visual double and binary</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Mizar A: .33  
Mizar B:4  
Alcor:3.99</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">a while ago</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Second star on handle of Big Dipper. This is the famous test of visual acuity. I can see the companion star (Alcor) under good conditions, although sometimes I have to tilt my glasses. In the telescope, it is easy to see that Mizor itself is a very close binary.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[Perseus Double Cluster](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_Cluster)</td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">NGC 884 and NGC 869</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Globular</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">4.3</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2007</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Easy to view with 6". Only one cluster fits in 16", but both can be viewed easily with 3" finder.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[Owl Cluster aka "ET Cluster"](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NGC_457)</td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">NGC 457</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Open Cluster</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">8.4</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">11/21/08</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This one of the nicest open clusters I have seen with the 16". There are several bright stars in an oval, and two bright stars which are the "eyes" of the owl or ET, whichever you care to imagine. There is also a rich smattering of dim background stars.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[Sirius](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sirius)</td>

<td width="9%" height="43"> </td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Multiple Star</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-1.46</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2/13/09</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Sirius is the brightest star in the night sky. It has a famous companion, "the pup", which is a relatively dim white dwarf which is rather difficult to spot. The pup was predicted due to the proper motion of Sirius by the mathematician Bessel. We took a quick look, out of curiosity, not expecting to see it. Because of the glare of Sirius, the only practical way of observing the "pup" is to block Sirius just outside the edge of the eyepiece. But you need to know which side the pup is on. We were not able to see it, but it still is worth a look if you are in the neighborhood. The pup is currently moving away from Sirius and will be at maximum elongation in 2025\. A third component has not yet been observed visually.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[Veil Nebula](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veil_nebula)</td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">NGC 6960, 6962, 6979, 6992,  6995</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Nebula</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">7.0</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">8/22/08</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Large, diffuse nebula spread through Cygnus. Observed through very nice 8 in telescope at ADK star party. I am not sure what part I observed, but it was probably the brightest loop, NGC 6960\. Later tried to observe with 16" at RPI, (9/08), the brighter half, was difficult to see anything under given conditions and narrow field of view, but Dave said one "rope" is usually visible passing through the brightest star.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[Christmas Tree Cluster](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christmas_Tree_Cluster)</td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">[NGC 2264](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christmas_Tree_Cluster)</span></td>

<td width="9%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Open Cluster and Nebula</span></td>

<td width="6%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2.6</span></td>

<td width="1%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">2/13/09</span></td>

<td width="119%" height="43"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The Christmas Tree Cluster contains the Cone Nebula, Fox Fur Nebula and Snowflake Cluster, however very few features are visible with amateur telescopes. Primarily one sees a large, sparse open cluster, which kindof sortof looks like a Christmas tree (with a bright star on top??). There is a one bright yellow star, which does appear to have some faint nebulosity around it. In actuality there are diffuse nebula filling the entire region. Large object, good to view in finder scope.</span></td>

</tr>

<tr>

<td width="17%" height="43">[PacMan Nebula](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacman_Nebula)</td>

<td width="9%" height="43">NGC 281</td>

<td width="9%" height="43">Diffuse Nebula</td>

<td width="6%" height="43"> </td>

<td width="1%" height="43"> </td>

<td width="119%" height="43"> </td>

</tr>

</table>

</center>
